  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7704afe1-0f68-447e-8d3f-c0a6aaab4b0a'
      });

  <span id="freeText790578673735238336" style="display:none"><b>Why is everyone talking about the ending of Sarah Pinborough's <i><b>Behind Her Eyes?</b></i></b><br /><br />Louise is a single mom, a secretary, stuck in a modern-day rut. On a rare night out, she meets a man in a bar and sparks fly. Though he leaves after they kiss, she’s thrilled she finally connected with someone.<br /><br />When Louise arrives at work on Monday, she meets her new boss, David. The man from the bar. The very married man from the bar…who says the kiss was a terrible mistake but who still can’t keep his eyes off Louise.<br /><br />And then Louise bumps into Adele, who’s new to town and in need of a friend, but she also just happens to be married to David. David and Adele look like the picture-perfect husband and wife, but then why is David so controlling, and why is Adele so scared of him?<br /><br />As Louise is drawn into David and Adele’s orbit, she uncovers more puzzling questions than answers. The only thing that is crystal clear is that something in this marriage is very, very wrong, but Louise can’t guess how wrong―and how far a person might go to protect their marriage’s secrets.</span>

<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    There is probably a spoiler effect to this answer, so continue reading at your own risk. <br /><br /> However, this book is being sold as something it is not and <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    There is probably a spoiler effect to this answer, so continue reading at your own risk. <br /><br /> However, this book is being sold as something it is not and that already has burned many of us, so I feel it is proper to warn people that it simply is not a pure psychological thriller. There is EXTREME paranormal ability involved. Ridiculous if you are not into that stuff.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1661962513?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1661962513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12345345711526199886">This might be one of the most difficult reviews I’ve had to write in the entire time I’ve been writing reviews. How does one convey their thoughts on just how addicting, intriguing, and consuming of a book this was, without exposing all the delicious spoilers that make it such a fun read? <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28965131.Behind_Her_Eyes' title='Behind Her Eyes by Sarah Pinborough' rel='nofollow noopener'>Behind Her Eyes</a> was the 200th book I’ve read this year, thus completing my Goodreads challenge early, so I guess you could say I’ve read quite a bunch of books in 2016. Out of all those books, this one will sta</span>
  <span id="freeText12345345711526199886" style="display:none">This might be one of the most difficult reviews I’ve had to write in the entire time I’ve been writing reviews. How does one convey their thoughts on just how addicting, intriguing, and consuming of a book this was, without exposing all the delicious spoilers that make it such a fun read? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28965131.Behind_Her_Eyes" title="Behind Her Eyes by Sarah Pinborough" rel="nofollow noopener">Behind Her Eyes</a> was the 200th book I’ve read this year, thus completing my Goodreads challenge early, so I guess you could say I’ve read quite a bunch of books in 2016. Out of all those books, this one will stand out for many reasons, but one of the largest would be due to the fact it is quite unlike anything I’ve read thus far in the genre.<br /><br />I can’t rave enough about how compulsive a read this was. I found myself wandering in and out of rooms to avoid people so that I could sneak in “just a few more pages”. The slow building suspense was gripping and so incredibly well written. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/457300.Sarah_Pinborough" title="Sarah Pinborough" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Pinborough</a> has become of my top 10 favorite authors this year and for good reason. Earlier this year I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6691674.The_Language_of_Dying" title="The Language of Dying by Sarah Pinborough" rel="nofollow noopener">The Language of Dying</a> and was blown away by her creation of something so beautiful yet disturbing; it absolutely wrecked me. Her talent can’t be confined to one genre; it’s too complex and excellent for that tiny box. She has taken the typical love triangle and made it anything but; there are multiple POVs and storylines intricately woven together to seem unrelated but, come on, we know better. She delicately brings each piece together until the precise moment she wants to drop the <b>#WTFthatending</b> moment. IMO there were really multiple twists that connect into one; the how/why/who was just as important separately as they were in one entity.<br /><br />I read quite a few early reviews on this book, and while some chose to include elements that I view as spoiler material, I almost wish I had seen them prior to reading this book. I believe my expectations would have been altered and I could have accepted this for what it was; an excellent book with a clever, mind-blowing twist that shouldn’t be confined by genre. The best way I know how to explain what I mean is that it doesn’t play by the usual rules of a psychological thriller. If you’ve seen anything yet about this book, you are clearly aware that there is a shocking ending with a whopper of a twist. The catch 22 is that, if this particular element I’m referring to was hinted at via genre description, the surprise aspect of the book is spoiled. The entire ending and twist are dependent on this aspect being kept secret, so you can see the dilemma I’m facing. I take full responsibility for this as it’s a personal problem based on my expectations of something filed in the “psychological thriller” genre.<br /><br />I can’t really say anything else without taking the fun out of reading this one; suffice it to say this is a <b>must read</b>. I think the most wonderful aspect of this book is that you don’t have to love how the plot works out to love reading the book. Whether you are drawn toward the ending or throw your book across the room, this is a story you must read if you call yourself a fan of any type of thriller. You might even need to read the beginning pages again for full clarity and comparison at just how beautifully <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/457300.Sarah_Pinborough" title="Sarah Pinborough" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah Pinborough</a> has slapped you across the face. This book buried into my brain so deeply that it was in all my waking thoughts and dreams for days; I couldn’t shake it. I’m just going to go ahead and let her take all my money; I’ll read anything she writes compulsively and will be sitting on pins and needles waiting for her next book.<br /><br /><b>Many thanks to Sarah and Flatiron Books for my treasured copy. She worked tirelessly to make sure my arc arrived and I’ll never forget that kindness. I’m paying it forward to Amy at Novelgossip so that we can discuss like ditzy school girls.</b> ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12345345711526199886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1813235209" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1813235209" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1813235209?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/31285838-behind-her-eyes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1813235209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1696673108161710058">A lot of readers are going to feel let down by this book. I'll try to explain without giving away any spoilers, but I will be talking about things revealed in the first few chapters.<br/><br/>Firstly, <b>the book gives up too much too soon</b>. It's about a beautiful, upper middle class couple - David and Adele - who on the outside appear to have the perfect marriage. Louise works for David, though her attraction to him, and her secret friendship with his wife, brings her closer and closer to the skeletons in th</span>
  <span id="freeText1696673108161710058" style="display:none">A lot of readers are going to feel let down by this book. I'll try to explain without giving away any spoilers, but I will be talking about things revealed in the first few chapters.<br /><br />Firstly, <b>the book gives up too much too soon</b>. It's about a beautiful, upper middle class couple - David and Adele - who on the outside appear to have the perfect marriage. Louise works for David, though her attraction to him, and her secret friendship with his wife, brings her closer and closer to the skeletons in their closet. The blurb itself screams "THINGS ARE NOT AS THEY APPEAR" and Louise is eventually going to find out just how crazy things really are. But we find out way before she does. <br /><br />A couple of chapters in, the author reveals that Adele is not all she first seems and is an expert at sneaky manipulation. The possibility that David is controlling and Adele may be the victim of domestic violence is shot down almost instantly and Pinborough (sort of) shows her hand. For the most part, there's <b>very little mystery</b>. Through Adele and Louise's alternating points of view, we know that Adele is mentally ill and Louise is incredibly naive.<br /><br />Comparisons to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> are pretty much guaranteed, though undeserved. What would <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/19288043.Gone_Girl" title="Gone Girl by Gillian Flynn" rel="nofollow noopener">Gone Girl</a> have been if Amy Dunne had given up all her secrets in the first couple of chapters? Far less impressive, I would guess.<br /><br />Louise behaves very foolishly throughout, to the point where she was kind of irritating. The plot pretty much relies on her idiocy. How can she be so stupid? Not only does she make a number of ridiculous choices that put her and her son in danger for silly reasons, but she also jumps to a huge conclusion in the later chapters of the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[How did she know that Adele dreamed of the "second door" just because Adele's sleeping habits were the same as hers? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />But most of all, I feel like many readers will feel let down by the twist at the end. I will be careful not to spoil anything, but let's just say that it is ludicrous. It's virtually impossible to guess because it's so outrageous and completely changes what you thought you were reading about. The marketing campaign for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28965131.Behind_Her_Eyes" title="Behind Her Eyes by Sarah Pinborough" rel="nofollow noopener">Behind Her Eyes</a> used the hashtag #WTFThatEnding to promote the book, and WTF, indeed. Though I prefer my WTFs to be a little more convincing.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1696673108161710058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1893004436" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1893004436" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1893004436?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1893004436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9961997715225616396"><b>*4.5 stars*...Sickeningly delicious storytelling!</b><br/><br/><b>Boom</b>. <i>That</i> ending. That "WTF-That-Ending" heard ‘round the world, or at least, the social media book-reading community. <br/><br/>It feels like this author just said, <b>“Know what? Screw this, I’m doin’ it”</b>, and then she <i>did</i> it. <br/>Seriously. She WENT for it.<br/><br/>It’s been a while since I’ve been legitimately shocked as a reader, and I don’t care how much this ending can be reduced down to utter nonsense, I’m embracing the hell out of it and you can’t stop me. <br/><br/>Becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText9961997715225616396" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 stars*...Sickeningly delicious storytelling!</b><br /><br /><b>Boom</b>. <i>That</i> ending. That "WTF-That-Ending" heard ‘round the world, or at least, the social media book-reading community. <br /><br />It feels like this author just said, <b>“Know what? Screw this, I’m doin’ it”</b>, and then she <i>did</i> it. <br />Seriously. She WENT for it.<br /><br />It’s been a while since I’ve been legitimately shocked as a reader, and I don’t care how much this ending can be reduced down to utter nonsense, I’m embracing the hell out of it and you can’t stop me. <br /><br />Because the fact is, when I swiped those last few virtual pages, my tired eyes narrowed, my offended guts twisted, my face took on a just-sucked-lemon contortion, and my lips curled into a tight little opening that spewed a whispered <i>
  <b>what the fuck?</b>
</i> declaration. And there is was. <br /><br />Sarah Pinborough’s writing is strong, and she paints a picture well without having to tell us the colors she’s using. There were no holes in this plot, no loose ends left untied. Everything made sense, even when it somehow didn’t. The perspectives shifted between characters, and the narratives sometimes switched from first and third person at random. It’s as though this story unveils itself from every angle possible, and yet still it goes and throws me off my feet. <br /><br />I know some readers couldn't get past some of the farfetched scenarios in this one, and I get it. I really do. I'm not one who readily ingests an over-the-top idea if there's not enough conviction behind it. In fact, I typically hate when I'm forced to suspend too much belief for an idea to "work". But this story was clever enough to become an exception. <br /><br />I can’t tell you details of the plot because I am your friend and I won’t ruin it for you. But I can tell you this: Soften your critical eye (if possible) when going into this one, so you can just enjoy the journey. Because it really is one hell of a ride...</span>
  <a data-text-id="9961997715225616396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1785447061" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785447061" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1785447061?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer3566832820422787714">2.5 stars<br/><br/><i>Behind Her Eyes</i> is very readable; I couldn’t put it down and I was constantly trying to figure out what was going to happen. However, once all was finally revealed, I came to the conclusion that I did not like this book. <br/><br/>It’s nearly impossible to write a summary of the events of this book without giving too much away, so I am just going to keep it as this: A man, his wife, and his secretary get caught up in a tangled web. <br/> <br/>I know that I am in the minority with my feelings about this one</span>
  <span id="freeText3566832820422787714" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br /><i>Behind Her Eyes</i> is very readable; I couldn’t put it down and I was constantly trying to figure out what was going to happen. However, once all was finally revealed, I came to the conclusion that I did not like this book. <br /><br />It’s nearly impossible to write a summary of the events of this book without giving too much away, so I am just going to keep it as this: A man, his wife, and his secretary get caught up in a tangled web. <br /> <br />I know that I am in the minority with my feelings about this one. I found it gimmicky and the twists ruined it for me. It's just not my cup of tea.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1894934156" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894934156" />
    <a title="Celina Grace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8471587-celina-grace"><img alt="Celina Grace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364762039p2/8471587.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1894934156?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celina Grace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celina Grace" href="/user/show/8471587-celina-grace">Celina Grace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1894934156" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4904925658537668607">I suppose I really shouldn't be surprised that, in an era where Donald Trump becomes president and Britain exits the European Union, that this book is lauded as one of the top psychological thrillers of the year. I could have overlooked the pedestrian prose, the utterly unlikeable (and unconvincing) characters and the plodding plot (done much better by other writers a billion times before) because I was looking forward to the twist of the year.<br/><br/>To give an indication of just quite how bad it actua</span>
  <span id="freeText4904925658537668607" style="display:none">I suppose I really shouldn't be surprised that, in an era where Donald Trump becomes president and Britain exits the European Union, that this book is lauded as one of the top psychological thrillers of the year. I could have overlooked the pedestrian prose, the utterly unlikeable (and unconvincing) characters and the plodding plot (done much better by other writers a billion times before) because I was looking forward to the twist of the year.<br /><br />To give an indication of just quite how bad it actually is - an insult to every reader's intelligence - I'll give you a few examples of how it could work in other books:<br /><br />Pride and Prejudice: Mr Darcy is actually really haughty and stand-offish because HE'S A ROBOT<br />To Kill a Mocking Bird: Atticus Finch is a really great lawyer because HE'S TIME-TRAVELLED FROM THE FUTURE<br />Jane Eyre: Mr Rochester is moody and troubled because HE'S A SHAPE-SHIFTING WEREWOLF<br /><br />I'm sure you get my point. This book is ridiculous and I suppose I should have known better, given that I'm currently living in a surreal dream-world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4904925658537668607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1821337195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3977593724615730507"><b> 2.5 Stars<br/> <br/>If I had known <u>then </u>what I know <u>now </u>I may not even have bothered reading this Novel as I felt it strayed from psychological thriller to Fantasy/Paranormal which didn't work for me. </b><br/><br/>I have a hard time suspending disbelief at the best of times in books and therefore stay away from novels where fantasy or magic realism play a role but I do like a good well written Psychological thriller and have read a couple this year that I really enjoyed. While Behind Her Eyes is unique and well writt</span>
  <span id="freeText3977593724615730507" style="display:none"><b> 2.5 Stars<br /> <br />If I had known <u>then </u>what I know <u>now </u>I may not even have bothered reading this Novel as I felt it strayed from psychological thriller to Fantasy/Paranormal which didn't work for me. </b><br /><br />I have a hard time suspending disbelief at the best of times in books and therefore stay away from novels where fantasy or magic realism play a role but I do like a good well written Psychological thriller and have read a couple this year that I really enjoyed. While Behind Her Eyes is unique and well written and there is no doubt the author holds your attention throughout but I did find a find myself having to seriously suspend disbelief and there was a lot of eye rolling not to mention a couple of choice words mouthed close to the end of the book for reasons that are best left unsaid.<br /><br />I would probably have rated the book 4 stars for suspenseful and original plot, great character development but what a let down the belief element was. I know I am in the minority on this one and so many readers have loved it but this is just my reaction to the book.<br /><br />I listened to this one on audio and the narration was excellent.<br /><br />An enjoyable read just not one for my favourites list.</span>

<div id="review_1932272477" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1932272477" />
    <a title="Dita " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26261386-dita"><img alt="Dita " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606101415p2/26261386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1932272477?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dita " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dita " href="/user/show/26261386-dita">Dita </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1932272477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer501082215358141462">If you're looking for a tight psychological thriller, please, keep looking. (And stop when you get to the brilliant Caroline Kepnes.) <br/><br/>I am a forgiving reader; give me a moderately cohesive story and some good characters and I will suspend disbelief and hang with you. <br/><br/>When you get me to buy in and then shamelessly jump the shark into contrived and cop-out paranormal bullshit, I'm out and I go hard. It's unfair to your reader.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1923958182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923958182" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923958182?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923958182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8374875577345595795"><div>
  <a href='https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-zmAI2pdy5vE/WLJvr_WbdyI/AAAAAAAALpg/SSKcO6mf5lUYpWrDrkH2kmsQVHlOKMA7QCLcB/s1600/gosling.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
    <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488090822ra/22079816.gif' width='320' height='134' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  </a>
</div><br/><br/>Umm, seriously? What did I just read?<br/><br/>Sarah Pinborough's new book, <b>
  <i>Behind Her Eyes</i>
</b> is one <i>crazy</i> book, one that at different times had me totally hooked, rolling my eyes, predicting (incorrectly) how the plot would be tied together, and then, ultimately, re-reading the last few chapters a few times to make sure what I thought happened actually did.<br/><br/>So, let's see how to review this. <br/><br/>"Secrets, secrets, secrets. People are filled to the brim with them if you look closely."<br/><br/>Louise is a s</span>
  <span id="freeText8374875577345595795" style="display:none"><div>
  <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-zmAI2pdy5vE/WLJvr_WbdyI/AAAAAAAALpg/SSKcO6mf5lUYpWrDrkH2kmsQVHlOKMA7QCLcB/s1600/gosling.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488090822ra/22079816.gif" width="320" height="134" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>Umm, seriously? What did I just read?<br><br>Sarah Pinborough's new book, <b>
  <i>Behind Her Eyes</i>
</b> is one <i>crazy</i> book, one that at different times had me totally hooked, rolling my eyes, predicting (incorrectly) how the plot would be tied together, and then, ultimately, re-reading the last few chapters a few times to make sure what I thought happened actually did.<br><br>So, let's see how to review this. <br><br>"Secrets, secrets, secrets. People are filled to the brim with them if you look closely."<br><br>Louise is a single mother to a young son. She works part-time as a secretary at a psychiatry office, and for the most part, spends her evenings caring for her son and drinking a little too much wine, and at times suffers from night terrors she can't explain. She'd love to meet a new man but doesn't really want to make the effort.<br><br>Then she meets him. Smart, funny, handsome, seems completely interested in her. They spend a somewhat drunken evening in a bar, and clearly there's chemistry between the two of them. After a passionate kiss, he flees, but she feels heartened that finally, someone special took an interest in her. Then on Monday, Louise discovers that this man is David, her new boss. Oh, and he's married, to a beautiful, elegant woman. Bollocks. <br><br>Louise bravely tries to soldier on despite her disappointment and David's occasionally flirtatious nature, but she is determined not to be one of <i>those</i> women. One day, while walking near her office, she (literally) runs into Adele, a beautiful, lonely woman clearly in need of a friend. And then, Louise quickly realizes Adele is David's wife. Adele starts to encourage Louise on ways to improve herself—cut back on the wine, quit smoking, join a gym.<br><br>When David's interest in Louise starts to intensify, she doesn't know what to do. She definitely has feelings for David, but she likes having Adele as a friend, even under the circumstances. She knows the secrets she's keeping from each of them are wrong, but she can't break up with either of them. And it appears both of them need her, in their own ways, as much as she needs them.<br><br>If you think you know what's going to happen from here, you're probably right—and you're utterly wrong. Pinborough combines elements of your typical love triangle and the story of the marriage that no one understands with some seriously bizarre, suspend-your-disbelief plot elements. When it works, the book practically hums with finesse and intrigue, and when it doesn't work, it's one of two things—you just can't wrap your head around what is allegedly happening, or you feel the book has fallen into such stereotypical territory it annoys you.<br><br>Ultimately, why this book worked for me (despite having to suspend my disbelief) is Pinborough's storytelling. These aren't likable characters, the plot jumps back and forth between narrators and time periods, and sometimes you wonder how the characters know what's going on. But Pinborough's writing mesmerized me, and the originality she demonstrates helps the positive outweigh the negative.<br><br>This will not be a book for everyone. But if you want to go on a crazy ride with some crazy characters, pick this one up. Because when a book comes with a hashtag, <b>
  <i>#wtfthatending</i>
</b>, you know you need to give it a try.<br><br>See all of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com">http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blo...</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8374875577345595795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1819796022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1819796022" />
    <a title="Maureen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13427823-maureen"><img alt="Maureen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1447766454p2/13427823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1819796022?book_show_action=true">Nov 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maureen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maureen" href="/user/show/13427823-maureen">Maureen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1819796022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5216376717250166469">Who's a clever girl then? No not me! The author Sarah Pinborough. When I say she's pulled a blinder with the conclusion of this book I'm not exaggerating.<br/><br/>Louise is a single mum on a rare night out when she meets a man in a bar. They share a drunken kiss and then he leaves, but Louise can't stop thinking about him, she felt a connection during their very short flirtation. When she arrives at the office after the weekend she's introduced to her new boss, and yes it's 'the man in the bar' David. It</span>
  <span id="freeText5216376717250166469" style="display:none">Who's a clever girl then? No not me! The author Sarah Pinborough. When I say she's pulled a blinder with the conclusion of this book I'm not exaggerating.<br /><br />Louise is a single mum on a rare night out when she meets a man in a bar. They share a drunken kiss and then he leaves, but Louise can't stop thinking about him, she felt a connection during their very short flirtation. When she arrives at the office after the weekend she's introduced to her new boss, and yes it's 'the man in the bar' David. It would be crazy to get involved with your boss especially as he's married right? Well Louise does become involved but oh boy she sure is going to regret it! <br /><br />When Louise accidentally bumps into Adele (David's wife) she finds herself pulled into a friendship with her that is bound to end in disaster, considering she's seeing David behind Adele's back.<br /><br />There was everything you could want in 'Behind Her Eyes'. It had an air of menace throughout in this twisted tale of love and obsession, and the plot was SO different, with even a touch of the supernatural. Just try to keep an open mind.<br /><br />I've read more than my fair share of psychological thrillers but I have NEVER come across such a complex and clever ending. I kept trying to pre-guess where this story was going but I had no chance - what a twist, I could never have created such a corker of a finish. Wow!<br /><br />*Thank you to Netgalley and Harper Collins UK for my ARC in exchange for a fair and honest review*<br /></span>

<div id="review_1855338465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1855338465" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1855338465?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1855338465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15144725259537924974">This is a character driven psychological thriller. It is well written enough to keep the reader engaged. The three main characters of Louise, David and Adele are unlikeable. Louise finds herself involved with David who turns out to be her new boss. She runs into his wife, Adele, and a cloying, claustrophobic, but close and secretive relationship develops between them. Since her divorce, Louise has had a stagnant and isolated personal life, and she needs the attention she has begun to receive. Da</span>
  <span id="freeText15144725259537924974" style="display:none">This is a character driven psychological thriller. It is well written enough to keep the reader engaged. The three main characters of Louise, David and Adele are unlikeable. Louise finds herself involved with David who turns out to be her new boss. She runs into his wife, Adele, and a cloying, claustrophobic, but close and secretive relationship develops between them. Since her divorce, Louise has had a stagnant and isolated personal life, and she needs the attention she has begun to receive. David is the first man she has a sexual affair with since her husband. Despite the guilt she feels, she gets drawn to and more closely entwined with Adele. A sinister and toxic image of Adele and David's marriage emerges. <br /><br />Louise has night terrors which Adele wants to help her with. She gives the mysterious notebook of the elusive Rob to guide her to counter those terrors. In a tale that takes in cats, fires and constant relocations of David and Adele, Louise may find that she has bitten off more than she can chew as she enters the uncharted waters of David and Adele's marriage. I am aware that many really love this novel, unfortunately I am not one of them. For me, the story developed does not segue well into the twists that unfold at the end. The dissonance I experienced between the rabbits pulled out of the hat at the close of the novel, felt like the author had arrived at calculated intellectual solutions which fail to match the revealed storyline. The character of David feels underdeveloped, and I did not have sufficient reasons to believe in his and Louise's relationship. However, I am sure the majority of readers will like this book. Many thanks to HarperCollins for an ARC. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15144725259537924974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Kaceey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13442817-kaceey"><img alt="Kaceey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463899458p2/13442817.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/33230997-behind-her-eyes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13442817-kaceey?shelf=top-reads-for-2017">top-reads-for-2017</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1820652897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12070632853509006202">Get ready for a wild ride! This was not what I expected, though I wasn’t even sure what was in store for me when I started this read. But I’d read enough reviews to know there was an off-the-charts spin at the end. Even forewarned, it still stopped me in my tracks!<br/><br/>Told from 2 points of view. <br/>Adele - married to David since she was a teenager. She is beautiful, ethereal, with a hint of vulnerability that draws people to her. Only she may have something hiding beneath the surface. (Well, of course!</span>
  <span id="freeText12070632853509006202" style="display:none">Get ready for a wild ride! This was not what I expected, though I wasn’t even sure what was in store for me when I started this read. But I’d read enough reviews to know there was an off-the-charts spin at the end. Even forewarned, it still stopped me in my tracks!<br /><br />Told from 2 points of view. <br />Adele - married to David since she was a teenager. She is beautiful, ethereal, with a hint of vulnerability that draws people to her. Only she may have something hiding beneath the surface. (Well, of course!)<br />Louise – adjusting to being newly single, raising her young son. Working as a secretary for Adele’s husband, David.<br /><br />When the paths of these three characters cross into a distorted love triangle, you just know that no one’s going to come out of this unscathed! One of them has an agenda! And one of them has vowed to never be stopped! But which one?<br /><br /><b>Oh this cannot end well!</b><br /><br />I think this is one of those books that it will either work for you and will absolutely love it. Or you will walk away saying <i>“what did I just read!”</i> Personally...It totally exceeded my expectations and I loved it! After reading so many thrillers, I wanted something original! Careful what you ask for! I got it...in spades! A completely different take on a domestic thriller. Keep an open mind and you’ll be pleasantly surprised!<br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer809073153603153475">What?  Ugh!  Seriously?<br/><br/>Oh my I don’t even know how to rate this one let alone review it! So for now 3.5 stars rounded down.<br/><br/>Did this novel pull me in?  Most definitely!  I was hooked right away and absolutely could not put this book down. It totally consumed me and I was constantly trying to figure out what the heck was going on!  Was it him…..was it her….and then the ending….oh brother, seriously!  That is what my thoughts were exactly after reading!<br/><br/>BEHIND HER EYES by SARAH PINBOROUGH was an int</span>
  <span id="freeText809073153603153475" style="display:none">What?  Ugh!  Seriously?<br /><br />Oh my I don’t even know how to rate this one let alone review it! So for now 3.5 stars rounded down.<br /><br />Did this novel pull me in?  Most definitely!  I was hooked right away and absolutely could not put this book down. It totally consumed me and I was constantly trying to figure out what the heck was going on!  Was it him…..was it her….and then the ending….oh brother, seriously!  That is what my thoughts were exactly after reading!<br /><br />BEHIND HER EYES by SARAH PINBOROUGH was an intriguing, gripping, exciting, and compulsive psychological thriller that grabbed my attention from the very first chapter and had me on the edge of my seat in anticipation for that ever so exciting and unforgettable ending that everyone seems to be talking about. Except after finishing reading this book I was a little disappointed about that ending. Sorry!<br /><br />And here is why…..trying not to reveal too much of why this didn’t work for me and spoiling the ending for someone else I will try to explain myself.  Simply I seen it coming and I didn’t want it to go there.  You might ask how did I see it coming?  Well, I have a really overactive imagination and like to see things in a different light and what might be seen as eccentric. If I didn’t see where the author was going with it would it have still been surprising? Absolutely!  Was it a good read?  Absolutely!<br /><br />I must say that BEHIND HER EYES is an absolutely brilliant title for this book!  Absolutely brilliant!  <br /><br />SARAH PINBOROUGH does deliver an extremely gripping story here that was well-written and had me totally engaged in the slow-building suspenseful story-line with a few good twists that had me questioning and guessing what was actually happening until I actually figured it all out.  I think if I didn’t figure it out it might have been a much better read for me!<br /><br />To sum it all up it was an entertaining, enjoyable, suspenseful, fast-paced, quick and easy read with a twist ending. Would recommend!!<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a><br /><br />Coulee: a term applied rather loosely to different landforms, all of which refer to a kind of valley.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2015035766" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2015035766" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2015035766?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008131975" href="/book/show/34098205-behind-her-eyes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2015035766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8667407052720356643"><br/>I read BEHIND HER EYES a few months ago when I received the paper ARC unexpectedly in my mail. Thank you Flatiron Books! I appreciate the hard work that you do to promote authors and new books. Having said that, I am always a bit leery of books that are sent out to the social media world with such grandiosity and heavy-handed publicity. Can't a great book get footing on its own? Sadly, maybe not. Oh well, never mind that thought. <br/><br/>I am somewhat of a realist, but I'm open-minded and curious about </span>
  <span id="freeText8667407052720356643" style="display:none"><br />I read BEHIND HER EYES a few months ago when I received the paper ARC unexpectedly in my mail. Thank you Flatiron Books! I appreciate the hard work that you do to promote authors and new books. Having said that, I am always a bit leery of books that are sent out to the social media world with such grandiosity and heavy-handed publicity. Can't a great book get footing on its own? Sadly, maybe not. Oh well, never mind that thought. <br /><br />I am somewhat of a realist, but I'm open-minded and curious about subjects like lucid dreaming, mainly for the psychological aspects that may pertain to a murder mystery. You are led as a reader to think this book is traveling the byways of memories, dreams, affairs and murders. The pages fly fast and I was so involved in this story - until the abrupt end. The publishers strongly encouraged all the ARC readers to discuss the book with the hypey #WTFthatending. Well, I guess that is an appropriate hashtag, but it goes either way. I detest the ending. Such a cheap gimmick. It's like having your mouth all set for a T-bone steak and it morphs right on the grill into a shape-shifting slice of frozen pizza. <br /><br />I know there are thousands of reviews out there on this book and my opinion appears to be in the minority. Not gonna lie, the ending of the story was like a sucker punch to the gut and I actually got angry. I tossed the book on the floor and didn't even bother writing a review for it. I felt used and abused as a reader.<br /><br />I live for plot twists. I love when authors write from different points of view. Heck, I want SHE LOVED PLOT TWISTS written on my tombstone. Not only that, but BEHIND HER EYES has a couple of unreliable narrators- my absolute favorite literary device! How could all these elements be in this one book, yet go so wrong?<br /><br />The ending of this book is more of a deus ex machina than anything else. Deus ex machina is a Latin term meaning "god out of the machine." It refers to an unexpected, artificial or improbable character, device or event introduced suddenly in a work of fiction to resolve a situation or untangle a plot. It is disappointing to me that a writer of Sarah Pinborough's caliber would end such a great story with a cheap plot device. There is barely a hint of where the book is going until the last few pages and then ridiculously, hideously its over. CRAZY TOWN!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8667407052720356643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1778230587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1778230587" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1778230587?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=sarah-pinborough">sarah-pinborough</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1778230587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17323621134121434347">"Love dies hard, you know?"<br/><br/>And that eye, fully dilated and widely on alert, says it all.<br/><br/>Now, let me just say that this one is not gonna be on everyone's radar. Having read Mayhem and The Language of Dying, Behind Her Eyes ventures into a deep psychological pond. The fish swimming there seem to glide against the tide of reality. You really wouldn't want to go wading into that pool of murky water on your own.<br/><br/>Louise, a single mom and a part-time employed secretary, dips her toes into that pond one </span>
  <span id="freeText17323621134121434347" style="display:none">"Love dies hard, you know?"<br /><br />And that eye, fully dilated and widely on alert, says it all.<br /><br />Now, let me just say that this one is not gonna be on everyone's radar. Having read Mayhem and The Language of Dying, Behind Her Eyes ventures into a deep psychological pond. The fish swimming there seem to glide against the tide of reality. You really wouldn't want to go wading into that pool of murky water on your own.<br /><br />Louise, a single mom and a part-time employed secretary, dips her toes into that pond one night. She shares a passionate kiss with a man at a crowded bar. That kiss still lingers as she comes to find out the next day that he is her new boss, David, the latest psychiatrist in her office. That kiss should also have come with a High Voltage warning. David and Louise can't get enough of one another and so it begins......<br /><br />And in walks Adele, David's beautiful wife. Strangely, Louise and Adele become friends and even share outings to a gym together. Let the games begin. David knows nothing of this bonding by the women. And Adele seems to know nothing about these two enamored fish. Oh, and Louise? She's certainly not saying much these days. <br /><br />This is a real cat and mouse tale told through chapters entitled "Then" and the shift back into the present. None of these characters are likeable for a multitude of reasons that will be revealed. But you find yourself unable to look away. Which one is more unstable than the other?<br /><br />Sarah Pinborough presents a story that is driven on a curvy road by these characters. I kept looking in the rearview mirror to see if I should have gotten off at the last exit. The last chapters will either hang your mouth open in shock or will tap on the brillance beacon. <br /><br />Sideline anything you've read before. This one dabbles in strange, very strange waters. So consider all things before taking this one on. The water's fine for some, but not for all. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17323621134121434347" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1923072170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1923072170" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1923072170?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=axis360">axis360</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=psychological-thriller">psychological-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=mystery-shelf">mystery-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1923072170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4995077483471047851">Behind Her Eyes by Sarah Pinborough is a 2017 Flatiron publication. <br/><br/>The reviews for this book were amazing for the most part, so I was eagerly awaiting my copy from the library. In the meantime, I got acquainted with the author by reading “Mayhem”, which was pretty good, and made me even more excited about delving into this one. <br/><br/>The book gets off to a sinister start because Adele and David are obviously having a hard time in their marriage. David appears to be the classic abusive control freak, </span>
  <span id="freeText4995077483471047851" style="display:none">Behind Her Eyes by Sarah Pinborough is a 2017 Flatiron publication. <br /><br />The reviews for this book were amazing for the most part, so I was eagerly awaiting my copy from the library. In the meantime, I got acquainted with the author by reading “Mayhem”, which was pretty good, and made me even more excited about delving into this one. <br /><br />The book gets off to a sinister start because Adele and David are obviously having a hard time in their marriage. David appears to be the classic abusive control freak, while Adele is the docile, reclusive, stay at home wife. <br /><br />Enter, Louise, David’s new secretary and suddenly a highly unusual triangle develops between the three of them. Louise suffers from night terrors and Adele helps her find a way to control them as their friendship continues to develop, despite the fact that Louise and David are carrying on together. As Louise gets more involved with the couple, she begins to understand there is something very wrong going on and finds herself caught in their web. <br /><br />If you have read any other reviews of this book, you will have no doubt heard about the surprise, ‘what just happened’ ending. While the majority of people have praised the conclusion,and I admit it was a total shock, I was mostly irritated by it, although as crazy as it was, it was also pretty chilling. <br /><br /> The buildup of suspense was very effectual, and the characters were well drawn for the most part. I was fully engaged in the story, which is certainly a mind trip, even before the ultimate shock ending, but I have to say that instead of feeling wowed, I was underwhelmed by the sucker punch twist. Still, I have to give the author kudos for pulling it off without a hitch, and I do ‘get’ why some people were impressed by it and why they have been raving about this book. <br /><br />The writing is stellar, but while I would love to say I really enjoyed this one, sadly I did not. So overall, this on gets a 2.5 rounded to 3. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4995077483471047851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2281139933" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281139933" />
    <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn"><img alt="Skyler Autumn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534857879p2/12859342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281139933?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skyler Autumn" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn">Skyler Autumn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12859342-skyler-autumn?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12859342-skyler-autumn?shelf=loath">loath</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281139933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4613904681522473150"><b> 2 Stars </b><br/><br/>Um No. I've had little think and I've come to the conclusion I did not like this book after all. Its very "readable" as I flew through it and enjoyed the read during the process, but afterwards it left a bad taste in my mouth and the more I pondered what I just read the more I was just irritated and felt cheated.<br/><br/>Behind Her Eyes is a perverse menage trois type deal between unhappily married husband and wife, Dave and Adele. And the single mother Louise that drunkenly kisses Dave one nigh</span>
  <span id="freeText4613904681522473150" style="display:none"><b> 2 Stars </b><br /><br />Um No. I've had little think and I've come to the conclusion I did not like this book after all. Its very "readable" as I flew through it and enjoyed the read during the process, but afterwards it left a bad taste in my mouth and the more I pondered what I just read the more I was just irritated and felt cheated.<br /><br />Behind Her Eyes is a perverse menage trois type deal between unhappily married husband and wife, Dave and Adele. And the single mother Louise that drunkenly kisses Dave one night and becomes close friends with Adele a few days later. I think Louise and my feelings on Louise can be summed up by this simple question Dave asks her <i>"Why, Why would you do that Louise?"</i> The entire novel was just me being baffled by the ridiculousness of Louise's behaviour, and frankly irritated by her childish manner. Every time she poked her nose into someone's business, or created unnecessary drama with her duplicitous behaviour, or just straight out didn't think about her child's safety I had to re-read the beginning chapter because I couldn't believe the author said this woman was 34 years old. NO she must be an idiot 20 year old or even teenager with how she behaved. <br /><br />The entire time Louise goes on about what a mess she's involved in then promptly declares she needs to find out more. Literally, all I could think is you're a single mother don't you have better things to be doing then nosing into someone else's marriage? Honestly the most psychotic person in this novel to me is Louise our supposed protagonist. Louise keeps saying how much she loves her baby boy but then continually says I can't deal with him today, then falls in love with a married alcoholic, and then puts herself in the middle of a crazy marriage that could spill back on her son's life. It's like my god and the mother of the year award goes to...<br /><br />All the characters were extremely unlikable. From a wet drip of a man Dave to ridiculous Louise to smug ass Adele. Honestly Adele was so irritating in her smugness declaring everything is going according to plan every two freaking minute. HOW?? How is anything going according to plan, it's all based on human interaction and error you can't predict people's behaviour (although apparently Adele can) but honestly if any other person was in Louise's shoes they would have blown up any of these so called "plans" because everything Louise did was absurdly illogical!! <br /><br />But the thing that mostly clinched this book as a disappointing read for me was the ending, the reveal the fucking ludicrous ending!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ THE ENDING!!! What the fuck. I was reading a thriller not a fantasy. Might as well have had a unicorn make a guest appearance if you want to completely dismiss logic. When someone tells you, you will in no way guess the ending. That is absolutely true because at no point will you think this book will leave the world of reality and become about Voodoo magic. WHAT A CHEAT ENDING!! I bought a thriller not a fantasy novel. Suddenly I'm suppose to go oh my god how did I not guess magic. It was magic all along!! LIKE REALLY?!?! It's suppose to be a domestic thriller not an episode of CHARMED!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall I wouldn't recommend this infuriating read to anyone that say's they want a thriller or specifically a domestic thriller novel because lets face it two-thirds in, this novel decides to jump ship genre-wise and leave it's readers thinking What the fuck?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4613904681522473150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2164102316" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164102316" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164102316?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=free-from-work">free-from-work</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164102316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3991762049131167187"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best mystery! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>some years back, i was at BEA with greg, and we were on line for something or other, and he’d wandered off to a nearby booth while i held our place. there was a gaggle of librarians behind me in line, and the boy-librarian was holding court, impressing all the girl-librarians* with his <i>game of thrones</i> knowledge by giving a highly detailed and booming synopsis of everything that happens in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62291.A_Storm_of_Swords__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___3_' title='A Storm of Swords (A Song of Ice and Fire, #3) by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Storm of Swords</a>, which i had</span>
  <span id="freeText3991762049131167187" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best mystery! what will happen?</b><br><br>some years back, i was at BEA with greg, and we were on line for something or other, and he’d wandered off to a nearby booth while i held our place. there was a gaggle of librarians behind me in line, and the boy-librarian was holding court, impressing all the girl-librarians* with his <i>game of thrones</i> knowledge by giving a highly detailed and booming synopsis of everything that happens in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62291.A_Storm_of_Swords__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___3_" title="A Storm of Swords (A Song of Ice and Fire, #3) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Storm of Swords</a>, which i had not yet read, but i knew from greg was the book with all the stuff and things. once i realized what was happening, i made the emphatic but unobtrusive clicking noise that means “come here now, please,” developed during many years of working in the bookstore trenches together, and the moment he returned to my side, i bounced outta earshot without a word of explanation. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509227821ra/24302211.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>in a perfectly executed choreography of facial expressions and ASL (which only one of us has studied, rendering it a gesture more decorative than useful), we established when it was safe for me to come back. which, for the record, was much longer than it should have taken - that nerd was on <i>fire</i> with detail.<br><br>i’ve since read the book and seen the show and i’m safe as safe can be from that particular spoiler-landmine, but the world is as full of twist endings as it is incautious booknerds, and with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28965131.Behind_Her_Eyes" title="Behind Her Eyes by Sarah Pinborough" rel="nofollow noopener">Behind Her Eyes</a>, pretty much the only thing i knew about it was that it was ALL ABOUT THE TWIST, and OMG, and i approached all reviews of it gingerly, not wanting to tempt fate or the spoiler monster.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509227901ra/24302215.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>i succeeded, but i wasn’t, of course, able to escape the knowledge that there <i>was</i> a twist, which comes with its own set of reader-distractions - finding myself subconsciously squinting for clues and developing theories while reading, which i 100% did not want to do, but every time i had to put the book down for any reason, my mind would slink into investigative/analytical mode and try to work out the twist without my consent. fortunately, investigative karen is a moron, and it’s a fast enough read that i was able to push most of life off to the side and gulp this down pretty quickly, and i figured out some things, but not that half-twist jab that comes after the main twist, which was a fun “hey now!” that tied up some lingering questions, but also created new ones.<br><br>here's the thing - in this case, the twist IS the book’s selling point. it’s a fun glossy pageturner; the book-equivalent of clickbait that sucks you right in (LGM) with its promise of YOU’LL NEVER GUESS, and YOU WON’T SEE IT COMING, and it’s an entertaining read, although peppered with implausible character behavior inspiring many “who would DO that?” eyerolls, but the momentum is all driving towards this promise of JUST YOU WAIT that, granted, delivers what it promises and is an unusual deviation from other books in this genre. however, it's not a tightly-fitting lid, and there's a lot left unresolved, sloppily explained, or significance overemphasized. paint color is just paint color, after all.<br><br>it's fun fluff, but i'll take fun over tedious any day. <br><br>* presumably.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3991762049131167187" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1855767624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1855767624" />
    <a title="Karl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1935255-karl"><img alt="Karl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588969235p2/1935255.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1855767624?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karl" href="/user/show/1935255-karl">Karl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1935255-karl?shelf=2016-12-books-bought">2016-12-books-bought</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1855767624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9208239050418141534">Perhaps "Behind Her Eyes" is a solid four and 1/2 stars, however the round up is necessary so as not to round down, in order to not give a false impression that this book is a fantastic read. Ms. Pinborough is a fun, sly and smart author when all is said and done.<br/><br/>So why quibble over that half a star ? To be honest I had some slight issues with the beginning of the book, which were overcome the further the story unfolded. My fear was what I call "The Gone Girl" syndrome, where you have this appre</span>
  <span id="freeText9208239050418141534" style="display:none">Perhaps "Behind Her Eyes" is a solid four and 1/2 stars, however the round up is necessary so as not to round down, in order to not give a false impression that this book is a fantastic read. Ms. Pinborough is a fun, sly and smart author when all is said and done.<br /><br />So why quibble over that half a star ? To be honest I had some slight issues with the beginning of the book, which were overcome the further the story unfolded. My fear was what I call "The Gone Girl" syndrome, where you have this apprehension that the author is just flat out messing with the reader.<br /><br />However Ms.. Pinborough is much more cleaver than your run of the mill word scribe. She has inserted enough clues into her narrative to give the reader the clues necessary not to feal swindled by unfolding events. <br /><br />The book is part family relationship drama with twosoms and threesoms, part mystery, part horror, layered and unfolded like an onion finally exploding with a creative and unique ending. Applause to Ms. Pinborough.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9208239050418141534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
